‎[31/12/2025, 8:19:07 AM] ~ Cobus 😎: This is our shift standards going forward, target is 152 loads per shift , supervisors this is your KPI combined with all the safety requirements.  Expected running hours per machine 9.6hrs ‎image omitted
[31/12/2025, 8:28:42 AM] ~ JSamo : Hi @⁨~Cobus 😎⁩ We acknowledge and agree with the shift standards going forward, including the target of 152 loads per shift, with supervisors being accountable for this KPI in full alignment with all safety requirements. We also take note of the expected 9.6 running hours per machine.

That said, for this target to be consistently achievable, there are several critical factors that need to be aligned and managed realistically:
	1.	Operator availability – We do not always operate with four operators per shift, which directly affects productivity and running hours. This needs to be clearly factored into planning and KPI expectations.
	2.	Loading and hauling cycle time – The cycle factor (loading, travel, tipping, and return) must be optimized and monitored, as it has a direct impact on achievable loads per shift.
	3.	Availability and reliability of loading equipment – Consistent availability of loading units is essential; any downtime or mismatch between loaders and hauling units will compromise the target.
	
We fully support the targets, but achieving them sustainably will require alignment on resources, equipment availability, and cycle efficiency, rather than focusing on output numbers alone.

Thank you 🙏
